201 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Brendsel v. Winchester Constr. Co.


No. 66, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


392 Md. 601; 898 A.2d 472; 2006 Md. LEXIS 255



May 10, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County.) Case No. CV-9858. Thomas G. Ross, JUDGE
Brendsel v. Winchester Constr. Co., 162 Md. App. 558, 875 A.2d 789, 2005 Md. App. LEXIS 68 (2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) entered a judgment that affirmed the trial court's judgment, which granted respondent contractor's petition to compel arbitration after ruling that the contractor had not waived its right to arbitration by seeking and obtaining an interlocutory mechanics' lien. Petitioner property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The contractor and the property owner entered into a contract for the renovation of a historic plantation house owned by the property owner. One contract section called for all disputes between the contractor and the property owner arising out of the contract to be decided by arbitration. Several disputes arose. Eventually, the property owner terminated the contract, and directed the contractor to remove its personnel and equipment. While the parties tried to work out their differences, the contractor became concerned because it had only 180 days after the work had been completed to petition for a mechanics' lien. To protect itself, it filed such a petition. Later, it filed a petition to compel arbitration. The property owner opposed the petition to compel arbitration and claimed that the contractor had waived its right to arbitration by seeking a mechanics' lien. The trial court disagreed with the property owner and the intermediate appellate court affirmed. On further review, the state's highest court found that under the circumstances, the contractor did not waive its right to compel arbitration merely by seeking and obtaining an interlocutory mechanics' lien.


OUTCOME: The intermediate appellate court's decision was affirmed.

 

202 of 744 DOCUMENTS



Trip Assocs. v. Mayor & City Council


No. 58, September Term, 2003


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


392 Md. 563; 898 A.2d 449; 2006 Md. LEXIS 254



May 9, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). John Carroll Byrnes, JUDGE.
Trip Assocs. v. Mayor & City Council, 151 Md. App. 167, 824 A.2d 977, 2003 Md. App. LEXIS 62 (2003)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT FOR ENTRY OF A JUDGMENT IN FAVOR OF THE PETITIONER. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners filed an action against appellees, a mayor and a city council, for judicial review of a decision of a board of municipal and zoning appeals restricting the number of days per week the owners could operate a nonconforming use. The trial court affirmed the board's decision. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed the trial court's judgment as to the restriction. The court granted the owners a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The owners operated a nightclub that had featured adult entertainment after hours twice a week since 1983. After a zoning inspector issued a code violation notice, the board held that the adult entertainment was a valid nonconforming use. It limited that use to two nights per week. The intermediate appellate court upheld the restriction based on Baltimore, Md., City Zoning Code § 13-406, which prohibited the expansion of certain nonconforming uses. It held that a temporal modification of a nonconforming use was an expansion of that use rather than a mere intensification of it. The court disagreed. It stated that Maryland cases had held that an intensification of a nonconforming use was permissible so long as the nature and character of that use was unchanged and was substantially the same. The court had consistently held that merely increasing the frequency of a nonconforming use was not an unlawful extension but an intensification. Increasing the number of nights on which adult entertainment was presented at the club here from two to five, for example, would be an intensification. The out-of-state cases relied upon by appellees were either distinguishable or unpersuasive.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the intermediate appellate court with instructions to it to reverse the trial court's judgment and to remand the case to the trial court for entry of a judgment in favor of the owners.


 

203 of 744 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 97, September Term, 2003


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


392 Md. 194; 896 A.2d 973; 2006 Md. LEXIS 187



April 14, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Williams v. State, 2008 Md. App. LEXIS 162 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., Dec. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Thomas Waxter, JUDGE.
Williams v. State, 152 Md. App. 200, 831 A.2d 501, 2003 Md. App. LEXIS 103 (2003)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted the State's petition for writ of certiorari, challenging the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which reversed defendant's convictions on appeal. Defendant had been convicted of the murder of a woman and related offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from his alleged murder of the victim to collect life insurance money. Central to the State's case was the testimony of an informant, who had occupied a cell adjacent to the one occupied by defendant when defendant was being held on the murder charge. The informant testified that defendant admitted to committing the murder as well as admitted to purchasing the murder weapon. The informant testified that he was getting nothing out of his testimony and that it was being given out of the goodness of his heart. Although unknown to the prosecuting attorney in defendant's case, the informant was a long-time paid and registered policy informant who had cooperated with the State's Attorney's Office in a number of cases and had received lenient treatment in the past for his information. The lower court had concluded that the State's Attorney's Office was on notice of the informant's status and failed to discharge its Brady obligation to disclose information favorable to defendant, with such failure to disclose tainting defendant's conviction. The court agreed that the State's non-disclosure was material to defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

204 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. State


No. 44, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


392 Md. 1; 895 A.2d 1024; 2006 Md. LEXIS 171



April 10, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Caroline County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case No. 05-K-05-006238. Karen A. Murphy Jensen, JUDGE.
Walker v. State, 388 Md. 404, 879 A.2d 1086, 2005 Md. LEXIS 537 (2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF CIRCUIT COURT FOR CAROLINE COUNTY VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO DISMISS APPEAL FROM DISTRICT COURT; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was charged with various sexual offenses and was found incompetent to stand trial. Petitioner filed a motion to dismiss the criminal charges. The Circuit Court for Caroline County (Maryland) affirmed the district court's denial of the motion. Petitioner's motion for certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented to the appellate court was whether the procedures set forth in Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc, §§ 3-106, 107, relating to the commitment of a defendant to a facility designated by the Department of Health and Mental Hygiene (DHMH) and to dismissal of the pending criminal charges, pass constitutional muster when DHMH has concluded that the defendant is not likely to achieve competence within a foreseeable time. Under what circumstances in that situation can the State Constitutionally continue to hold the defendant in confinement? At what point must the pending charges be dismissed? The appellate court held that it was unable to address the issue presented because petitioner chose the wrong vehicle for presenting the issue to the appellate court. The order denying relief from continued confinement was not a final order in the pending criminal case and therefore, was not appealable as a final judgment. The appellate court noted that petition could have effectively presented the issues of release from confinement and dismissal of the criminal charges though a petition for habeas corpus or a petition for release under Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. § 7-507.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was vacated and the case was remanded with instruction to dismiss the appeal from the district court.

 

205 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Burch v. United Cable TV of Balt. Ltd. P'ship


No. 62, September Term, 2003


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


391 Md. 687; 895 A.2d 980; 2006 Md. LEXIS 169



April 7, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Kaye A. Allison, JUDGE.
Burch v. United Cable, 377 Md. 111, 832 A.2d 204, 2003 Md. LEXIS 624 (2003)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE PETITIONERS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) entered a judgment that affirmed a trial court's ruling that granted defendant cable television provider's motion to vacate a permanent injunction, the effect of which was to allow the cable television provider to collect future late fees in accordance with a law that the Maryland General Assembly recently enacted. Plaintiff cable customers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The cable customers filed a class action lawsuit against the cable television provider that challenged a five-dollar per month late fee. The trial court entered an injunction that enjoined the cable television provider from collecting late fees. The highest court of review then ruled that the cable television provider could only charge the interest rate allowed under Md. Const. art. III, § 57. In response to that decision, the Maryland General Assembly enacted Md. Code Ann., Com. Law § 14-1315 (Repl. Vol. 2002), which was became effective on a particular date and increased the maximum allowable late fees that could be collected on specified consumer contracts. Eventually, the cable television provider requested that the trial court vacate the permanent injunction entered a few years earlier. The trial court, to comply with the new law, dissolved the injunction. The intermediate appellate court affirmed. On further review, the highest court of review found that it should not address a constitutional claim raised by the cable customers because that claim had not been raised in the trial court and the trial court had the authority to dissolve the injunction.


OUTCOME: The intermediate appellate court's judgment was affirmed.

 

206 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Abeokuto v. State


No. 129, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


391 Md. 289; 893 A.2d 1018; 2006 Md. LEXIS 73



February 13, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Abeokuto v. Warden, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 61426 (D. Md., July 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Death Penalty - Circuit Court for Baltimore County. Case # 03 CR 2127. Thomas J. Bollinger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY AFFIRMED AS TO ALL CONVICTIONS; SENTENCING VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR A NEW SENTENCING PROCEEDING; COSTS TO BE PAID BY BALTIMORE COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) judgment convicting him, after a bench trial, of murder, assault, kidnapping, and related offenses, and sentenced him to death. He argued 17 issues on appeal, most prominently that he had not knowingly and voluntarily waived his rights to jury trial and jury sentencing and that various items of evidence should have been suppressed. He also challenged certain sentencing rulings.


OVERVIEW: Abundant evidence, much of it supplied by defendant in statements made before he was in custody and in clothing that he consensually turned over to police, supported defendant's conviction of having kidnapped and brutally killed his girlfriend's daughter and seeking to extort money for her return. He argued, however, that he had not knowingly and voluntarily waived his rights to jury trial and sentencing. The court agreed with the State as to the waiver of jury trial, because the situation had been carefully explained to defendant and the court had just finished a detailed examination of defendant's mental state in finding him competent to be tried. When defendant waived jury sentencing nine weeks later, far fewer inquiries were made as to his understanding, despite the fact that he remained heavily medicated. It was not clear from the record that he understood his choices. Defendant's Fourth and Fifth Amendment challenges were either unpreserved or without merit. Finally, in dicta, the court directed that at resentencing the trial court should avoid illegal sentence increases and merge defendant's convictions of two types of kidnapping offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions in all respects but vacated the sentencing orders. It remanded the matter for a new sentencing proceeding.

Dep't of Natural Res. v. Heller


No. 23, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


391 Md. 148; 892 A.2d 497; 2006 Md. LEXIS 69; 24 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 169



February 9, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Somerset County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. J. Owen Wise, Judge.
Heller v. Dep't of Natural Res., 161 Md. App. 299, 868 A.2d 925, 2005 Md. App. LEXIS 17 (2005)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR SOMERSET COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Special Appeals Court (Maryland) entered a judgment that found, in contradiction to the findings of the Administrative Law Judge (ALJ), that respondent claimant made protected disclosures regarding alleged fiscal improprieties and that the ALJ erroneously precluded him from introducing evidence relevant to the merits of the underlying sexual harassment claim. Petitioner employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was hired to work as a manager at a marina run by petitioner state natural resources department. His responsibilities involved making the marina profitable, especially since it had posted a loss the previous year. Thereafter, sexual harassment allegations were leveled against him. The claim was investigated and the claimant was permanently transferred to another location as a result. He then filed a whistleblower action against the state natural resources department and alleged that the disciplinary action was not a consequence of the sexual harassment claim, but was retaliatory for alleged protected disclosures he made about purported fiscal irregularities in the marina's operating budget. An administrative law judge (ALJ) found that he had not proven that he had made the purported disclosures and barred him from presenting evidence about the merits of the harassment claim. The special appeals court disagreed with the ALJ. On further review, the court of last resort found that the claimant had not proven he made the allegedly protected disclosure and the sexual harassment claim evidence was irrelevant to the disciplinary motive.


OUTCOME: The special appeals court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with directions to affirm the trial court's judgment.

Sec'y, Dep't of Pub. Safety & Correctional Servs. v. Demby


No. 42, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


390 Md. 580; 890 A.2d 310; 2006 Md. LEXIS 12



January 17, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Somerset and Circuit Court for Washington County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Daniel M. Long and Frederick C. Wright, III, JUDGE. Civil Nos. 19-C-02-008762, 19-C-03-00856, 21-C-02-014860, 21-C-02-14841,19-C-02-008572.
Demby v. Sec'y, Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr. Serv., 163 Md. App. 47, 877 A.2d 187, 2005 Md. App. LEXIS 84 (2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted the petition for writ of certiorari filed by petitioner, the Secretary of Public Safety and Correctional Services, and the cross-petition for the same filed by respondents, five inmates. The appeal involved the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which reversed the decisions of the relevant trial courts that dismissed the inmates' grievances, which alleged various regulatory amendments were ex post facto laws.


OVERVIEW: The regulations at issue concerned special project diminution of confinement credits that were awarded to inmates for being double celled. The inmates asserted that the amendments were ex post facto laws, in violation of the United States Constitution and Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 17. All of the inmates had been eligible for special project credits for double celling but were precluded from such credits as a result of the amendment set forth in Md. Code Regs. 12.02.06.05 (2002). Based on the amendments, the inmates were not eligible for the special project credits because their sentences included a disqualifying offense such as carjacking or murder. The court found that the amendments at issue were more than mere guides and were, in fact, substantive in nature and, therefore, were within the scope of the ex post facto clauses at issue as the adoption of the amendments immediately prohibited various categories of inmates from receiving special housing credits for double celling. In applying the ex post facto analysis to the regulation amendment, the court agreed with the lower court that it was an ex post facto law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision.

 

209 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Illiano


No. 28, September Term, 2005,


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


390 Md. 265; 888 A.2d 329; 2005 Md. LEXIS 747



December 16, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: MVA v. Illiano, 387 Md. 465, 875 A.2d 769, 2005 Md. LEXIS 382 (2005)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CARROLL COUNTY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE MOTOR VEHICLE ADMINISTRATION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Maryland Motor Vehicle Administration (MVA), sought to suspend respondent driver's driver's license. An administrative law judge (ALJ) found that the MVA had reasonable grounds to suspend his license for one year under Md. Code, Md. Code Ann., Transp. I, § 16-205.1(b)(1)(i)(2)(B). The Circuit Court of Carroll County, Maryland, reversed. The MVA appealed.


OVERVIEW: The driver stopped her car on the shoulder of a highway about 10 feet behind a police officer. The officer exited his car to check on the well-being of the persons in the driver's car. The ALJ finding that the officer possessed reasonable grounds to justify the detention of the driver was supported by substantial evidence and sustained. Under Md. Code, Md. Code Ann., Transp. I, § 16-205.1(b)(2), after having made what was characterized as a routine stop, it was reasonable for the officer to further detain the driver to administer a chemical breath test based upon facts developed after the initial stop. The facts included that the inside of the car had a strong odor of alcohol, the driver said that she had two drinks and should not be driving, and the driver's eyes were bloodshot and glassy and her speech was slurred. The ALJ determination that the officer had reasonable grounds to detain the driver for driving under the influence of alcohol and to request that she submit to a breath test was supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed the judgment of the lower court and directed the lower court to uphold the decision of the ALJ.

 

210 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Grandison v. State


No. C16, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


390 Md. 412; 889 A.2d 366; 2005 Md. LEXIS 748



December 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Grandison v. Maryland, 549 U.S. 956, 127 S. Ct. 382, 166 L. Ed. 2d 275, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 7565 (Oct. 10, 2006)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion denied by Grandison v. State, 425 Md. 34, 38 A.3d 352, 2012 Md. LEXIS 78 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Evans v. State, 389 Md. 456, 886 A.2d 562, 2005 Md. LEXIS 649 (2005)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR SOMERSET COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In his fifth appeal of a death sentence imposed after his conviction of first-degree murder for hire, defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Somerset County (Maryland) that denied his motions for a new trial, to correct sentence, and to reopen his post-conviction proceeding. He argued the relief was mandated by Brady violations and challenged the constitutionality of the death penalty statute and his death eligibility.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been convicted of hiring another to kill potential witnesses against him. He was eventually sentenced to death under the former death penalty statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§ 412 and 413 (1982). The court held, first, that given the overwhelming evidence of guilt, defendant had not established that certain evidence that he claimed had not been made available to him would have made any difference in his outcome, so there was no Brady violation. Second, there was no Sixth Amendment violation in the procedure under which, after finding facts of death eligibility beyond a reasonable doubt, the jury then went on to exercise its judgment in weighing aggravating and mitigating circumstances looking to a preponderance of the evidence. Finally, the plain language of the statute indicated that although for the most part only principals were death eligible, there was an exception for those who procured murders for hire.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Weller


No. 20, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


390 Md. 115; 887 A.2d 1042; 2005 Md. LEXIS 735



December 12, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Carroll County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case # C-04-041186 AA. Michael M. Galloway, JUDGE.
MVA v. Weller, 387 Md. 462, 875 A.2d 767, 2005 Md. LEXIS 330 (2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CARROLL COUNTY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR ENTRY OF JUDGMENT AFFIRMING THE AGENCY DETERMINATION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Maryland Motor Vehicle Administration, was granted certiorari with regard to two questions it presented for review as to the decision of the Circuit Court of Carroll County (Maryland), which reversed the decision of an Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) that suspended respondent drier's driving privileges following a driving incident where the driver refused to submit to a chemical breath test.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped the car in which the driver was operating after seeing the car cross over a set of double yellow lines on the road. The driver failed the field sobriety tests administered and refused to take a chemical breath test. The driver was issued an order of suspension, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1 (1977, 2002 Repl. Vol., 2005 Supp.), for refusing to take the chemical breath test. The ALJ suspended the driving privileges of the driver for one year. The trial court vacated the one year suspension upon determining that the ALJ failed to give proper consideration to the driver's employment as an insurance adjuster and that driving was required by his job, that the driver's prior alcohol offense was over eight years ago, nor that the ignition interlock was an available option on the driver's personal vehicle. The court held that the trial court erred in considering the issue of the admissibility of the preliminary breath test result before the agency since no objection to its admissibility was made. Further, the trial court improperly substituted its judgment for that of the ALJ in that substantial evidence existed to support the suspension.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for that court to enter a judgment affirming the agency determination.

 

212 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Kane v. Bd. of Appeals


No. 29, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


390 Md. 145; 887 A.2d 1060; 2005 Md. LEXIS 737



December 12, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Kane v. Bd. of App. of Prince George's, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 4363 (U.S., June 5, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Case # CAL00-18995. C. Phillip Nichols, JUDGE.
Kane v. Bd. of Appeals, 387 Md. 465, 875 A.2d 769, 2005 Md. LEXIS 381 (2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONERS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A fire department issued citations to plaintiffs, property owners, for fire code violations. The owners appealed the citations to a board of appeals, to the trial court, and to the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland). Those bodies found that the citations were properly issued. The owners petitioned for a writ of certiorari, which the state supreme court granted.


OVERVIEW: The fire department cited the owners for fire hazards found in rented apartments. The owners argued that the language of Prince George's County, Md., Code § 11-162 precluded issuing citations to or otherwise penalizing the owners of leased premises for the conduct of their renters involving the renters' personal property. The state supreme court held that the qualifying clause "responsible for the condition or violation" only modified the term "other person." As a result, there were five separate persons or entities who can be cited: (1) the owner, (2) the operator, (3) the occupant, (4) the agent, or (5) other person responsible for the condition or violation. Thus, the statute allowed the fire department to cite the property owners. The owners also argued that Prince George's, Md., County Code § 11-162 as applied violated their due process rights. The appellate court found that the statute, as applied, did not ask the property owners to inspect or even monitor every tenant's actions. It primarily requires that, upon notification of a violation, the landlord had to ensure that the violation was corrected. The appellate court found that this was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

213 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Boyd v. Bell Atlantic-Maryland, Inc.


No. 11, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


390 Md. 60; 887 A.2d 637; 2005 Md. LEXIS 733



December 8, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case No. CAL 99-21004. Steven I. Platt, JUDGE.
Boyd v. Bell Atl., 386 Md. 180, 872 A.2d 46, 2005 Md. LEXIS 200 (2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO ENTER JUDGMENT (1) VACATING ORDER OF CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY BARRING CLASS MEMBERS FROM PURSUING CLAIMS IN OTHER FORA, (2) OTHERWISE DISMISSING APPEAL, AND (3) REMANDING CASE TO CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID 3/4 BY PETITIONERS AND 1/4 BY RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted plaintiffs, consumer and business customers, certiorari to review the decision of the Special Court of Appeals (Maryland), which dismissed plaintiffs' appeal that challenged a trial court decision approving a settlement of two consolidated class actions against defendants, a provider of telephone service and the Maryland Public Service Commission, over the objections of some plaintiffs. The case involved late fees charged.


OVERVIEW: The settlement gave final approval to a settlement that reserved the amount of $ 12,500,000, which was subject to division between a cy pres group of customers that likely included most of the class members and the attorneys. The lower court dismissed the appeal as one not allowed by law in that it concluded that the settlement was not a final, appealable decision. Plaintiff asserted that though the order approving the settlement did not finally resolve how much the class members or anyone else will actually receive from the settlement, it nonetheless constituted a final judgment. Alternatively, plaintiffs noted that one aspect of the order was a directive barring class members from asserting claims encompassed by the settlement in any other court or tribunal, which was in the nature of an injunction, which did permit an appeal. The court agreed that the order was not an appealable final judgment but that the portion barring further suit was in the nature of an interlocutory injunction that was immediately appealable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and remanded the case to that court with instructions to enter a judgment vacating the trial court's order barring class members from pursuing claims in other fora and that dismissed the appeal. The court also remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

214 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Benson v. State


No. 7, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


389 Md. 615; 887 A.2d 525; 2005 Md. LEXIS 728



December 7, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Balitmore City pursuarnt to certiorari to the court of Special Appeals. Thomas E. Noel, JUDGE.
Benson v. State, 386 Md. 180, 872 A.2d 46, 2005 Md. LEXIS 199 (2005)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court issued a writ of certiorari to decide the appellate issues raised by appellants, two payers, with regard to the judgment of the Baltimore City Circuit Court (Maryland) in favor of appellees, the State of Maryland, its prison system, a prison inmate fund, and other entities. Appellants asserted constitutional and statutory violations arising from the State receiving a commission from collect telephone calls made by inmates.


OVERVIEW: The non-emergency telephone calls made by the inmates were assessed a specific rate, with the State receiving a commission on each call from the telephone company. Appellants, who received and paid for the calls, asserted that such commission remitted to the State was illegal under Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 14, Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 8, and Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24, as well as violated the Maryland Consumer Protection Act (CPA), Md. Com. Law § 13-301 (1975, 2005 Repl. Vol.). The court found that the trial court erred in dismissing appellants' claims for failing to comply with the Maryland Tort Claims Act (MTCA), Md. State Gov't § 12-101 et seq. (2005), because a claim under Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 14 was not compensable in monetary damages and meeting the requirements of the MTCA was not necessary. The court held that the commission was within the scope of Article 14 because it was a charge imposed by the State that the Maryland Legislature consented to by enacting the Inmate Welfare Fund, Md. Code Ann., Corr. Serv. § 10-502 (1999).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

215 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Lawson v. State


No. 12, September Term, 2005


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


389 Md. 570; 886 A.2d 876; 2005 Md. LEXIS 663



November 28, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Case # CT021375X.) William B. Spellbring, Jr., JUDGE.
Lawson v. State, 160 Md. App. 602, 865 A.2d 617, 2005 Md. App. LEXIS 4 (2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMING CONVICTIONS OF RAPE, ATTEMPTED RAPE AND ASSAULT IS REVERSED AND THE CASE IS REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT FOR A NEW TRIAL. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari to defendant's appeal from that portion of a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland that affirmed his conviction of rape of a child and related offenses. He argued, most prominently, that a social worker's testimony regarding the child's statements was improperly admitted under Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 11-304 (2001 & 2005 Supp.) and that improper statements in closing argument required a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The child testified at defendant's trial, but the State also presented a county-employed social worker as a corroborating witness, and she testified to the child's statements to her soon after the last incident of alleged abuse. The court held that since Maryland's whole child protection scheme relied on investigations by human services professionals, and since the social worker fell under that definition, she was certainly within the category of investigators who were allowed to testify regarding a child's statement of sexual abuse under § 11-304. There was no confrontation issue because the child testified at trial and was available for cross-examination. The court nonetheless found it necessary to reverse defendant's convictions on other grounds. During closing argument, particularly, the prosecutor had used a "golden rule" argument and had made many inflammatory remarks and references to matters not in evidence, and the trial court had done almost nothing to stop her. Cumulatively, these improper remarks were likely to have prejudiced defendant's outcome and therefore constituted plain error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court and remanded the case to that court with directions to reverse the judgment of the trial court and to remand the matter to that court for a new trial.

 

216 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Massey v. Sec'y, Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr. Servs.


No. 142, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


389 Md. 496; 886 A.2d 585; 2005 Md. LEXIS 656



November 21, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Allegany County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Specials Appeals. Timothy W. Finan, JUDGE. Case No. C-02-021277.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On its own initiative, the court granted certiorari, before review by an intermediate court, to plaintiff inmate's appeal of a Circuit Court for Allegany County (Maryland) decision upholding the validity of Directives 105-4 and 105-5 issued by defendant Secretary, Maryland Department of Public Safety and Correctional Services (DPSCS). The inmate argued that the directives were regulations within the meaning of Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 10-101.


OVERVIEW: Md. Code Ann., Corr. Serv. §§ 2-109 and 3-205 authorized DPSCS and its Division of Correction to issue administrative directives to assure smooth running of corrections operations. Those statutes did not, however, exempt them from the rule-making procedural requirements set forth at Md. Code Ann., State Gov't §§ 10-101 through 10-117. An inmate challenged the directives pursuant to which he had been deprived of credits, but an administrative tribunal and the trial court held that the rules were mere internal procedures, not subject to the statutory rule-making requirements. The court held that because of the due process implications of increasing a term of incarceration, such rules could never be mere internal procedures. They were rules within the meaning of Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 10-101, and were invalid because they had not been properly promulgated. To avoid chaos in prison administration, the court delayed issuance of its mandate for 120 days, to allow DPSCS to bring its rule-making procedures into conformity with the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the matter to that court with instructions to reverse the administrative decision and to direct the inmate grievance office to conduct a hearing on the inmate's complaint. It further directed that its mandate not issue for 120 days, to permit DPSCS to adopt appropriate rules in accordance with administrative procedural statutes.

Evans v. State


Misc. No. 18, September Term, 2004, Misc. No. 3, September Term, 2005

Post-conviction proceeding at, Application granted by, Stay granted by Evans v. State, 2006 Md. LEXIS 54 (Md., Feb. 6, 2006)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Injunction granted at Evans v. Saar, 2006 Md. LEXIS 51 (Md., Feb. 6, 2006)

Post-conviction relief denied at, Remanded by Evans v. State, 396 Md. 256, 914 A.2d 25, 2006 Md. LEXIS 836 (2006)
Related proceeding at Evans v. State, 2015 Md. App. LEXIS 772 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., Oct. 23, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Misc. No. 3

Motion to Correct Illegal Sentence-Baltimore County. Christian M. Kahl, JUDGE.

Misc. No. 18

Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County pursuant to the Unopposed Motion to Stay Warrant of Execution. (Baltimore County)Case No. 83-CR-2339. John Grason Turnbull, II, JUDGE
Evans v. State, 382 Md. 248, 855 A.2d 291, 2004 Md. LEXIS 453 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted direct review to orders of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) denying defendant's Md. R. 4-345 motions to correct illegal sentence, his tenth and eleventh challenges to a death sentence imposed on him after being found guilty of a double murder for hire. He particularly argued that federal constitutional case law invalidated the burden of proof used by jurors in the Md. Code Ann., Crim. § 2-303, weighing process.


OVERVIEW: The court first noted that defendant's constitutional challenges probably should not have been raised as motions to correct an illegal sentence. Nonetheless, it reviewed the merits of his claims. First, the aggravating factors the State planned to argue did not have to be set forth in the original murder indictment, so long as defendant had ample notice of the charges and what he would need in the way of a defense. The Fifth Amendment's grand jury requirement did not apply to the states, and the Sixth Amendment and Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 21 simply required fair notice. Defendant also argued that the decisions of the nation's highest court in Apprendi v. New Jersey and Ring v. Arizona invalidated earlier case law holding that so long as the aggravating factors justifying the death penalty were found, by a jury, to exist beyond a reasonable doubt, the jury could then apply a preponderance of the evidence standard in weighing the aggravating factors against the mitigating factors. The court dismissed the argument with no discussion, seeing no reason to modify its earlier rulings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

 

218 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Harvey v. Marshall


No. 109, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


389 Md. 243; 884 A.2d 1171; 2005 Md. LEXIS 600



October 14, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Case # 102756 John P. Miller, JUDGE.
Harvey v. Marshall, 158 Md. App. 355, 857 A.2d 529, 2004 Md. App. LEXIS 127 (2004)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari to plaintiff custodial father's appeal from an affirmance by the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland of a decision upholding third-party defendant agency's decision denying the father's request that it extinguish, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-1038(b) (2004), child support arrearages assigned to the State by nominal defendant mothers of his children.


OVERVIEW: The father had accumulated large child support arrearages, assigned to the State by the mothers when they were granted welfare benefits, by the time he assumed custody of his children. He sought forgiveness of the arrearages, arguing that it was in the children's best interest that he should use his income to support them, rather than paying the State. The court held that while the father claimed to request that the agency exercise its § 5-1038(b) discretion to extinguish an order that related to facts that no longer existed, he was really, by the plain language of § 5-1038 and Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 12-104 (2004), seeking a retroactive modification of his child support obligation, something the latter statute forbade. The father also challenged the agency's refusal to exercise its discretion under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 10-112 (2004) to grant relief from arrearages in appropriate cases, arguing that it was an arbitrary and capricious decision based solely on the State's financial interest rather than the children's best interest. The court held that the legislature had determined, in establishing the enforcement process, that those considerations were entirely appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Baker v. State


No. 132, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


389 Md. 127; 883 A.2d 916; 2005 Md. LEXIS 586



October 3, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Baker v. Saar, 402 F. Supp. 2d 606, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 31324 (D. Md., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motions to Correct Illegal Sentence and to Reopen Postconviction Proceedings Death Penalty. Circuit Court for Harford County. Case # 12-K-92-000088. Emory A. Plitt, Jr., JUDGE.
Baker v. State, 383 Md. 550, 861 A.2d 48, 2004 Md. LEXIS 612 (2004)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Harford County (Maryland) denying, without a hearing, the inmate's motion to correct an illegal sentence where the inmate had been sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Principally relying on a statistical study commissioned by the governor examining the implementation of the death sentencing scheme, the inmate argued in his motion to correct an illegal sentence pursuant to Md. R. 4-345(a) that his death sentence was imposed in a racially-biased and geographically-biased manner. He argued the death penalty statute was applied to him in violation of the Eighth Amendment and the Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 16 and Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 25 prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment and in violation of his equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24. The motion was proper only if the alleged illegality occurred in the sentence itself or if, in a capital case, where the basis of the constitutional argument in support of the alleged error was based on a decision or decisions of the United States Supreme Court. There was no direct and specific evidence to suggest that the inmate's sentence was surrounded by impropriety of any kind. The case did not fit within the capital sentencing exception to Md. R. 4-345(a) because the inmate relied on a study rather than on a Court decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

220 of 744 DOCUMENTS


PSC v. Wilson


No. 133, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


389 Md. 27; 882 A.2d 849; 2005 Md. LEXIS 547



September 13, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant ot certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Joseph H.H. Kaplan, JUDGE.
PSC v. Wilson, 385 Md. 161, 867 A.2d 1062, 2005 Md. LEXIS 53 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari before an intermediate court considered an appeal by defendants, the Maryland Public Service Commission and its chairman, from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) that sustained plaintiff former state employee's appeal from her termination by the chairman and from a later termination by act of a majority of the commission.


OVERVIEW: The at-will management employee was terminated by the chairman without being given a reason, as were a number of others. The chairman later said he had been dissatisfied with her work at times but had not terminated her for misconduct. The court held, first, that reading Md. Code Ann., State Pers. & Pens. § 11-305 (2004) and various statutes dealing with utility regulation together, it was clear that the full commission, not the chairman, was the appointing authority so, in the absence of a delegation, the first termination was illegal. A majority of the commission effected the second termination, however, and that was upheld. The employee had not established that she was fired for misconduct, understood generally to mean serious violations of standards, and without such a showing, she was not entitled to the pre-termination procedures set forth at Md. Code Ann., State Pers. & Pens. § 11-106 (2004). Finally, although exhaustion of remedies rules were sometimes relaxed in cases involving constitutional challenges, the employee's challenges to the review procedures of Md. Code Ann., State Pers. & Pens. § 11-113 (2004) did not claim facial invalidity, so exhaustion was required.


OUTCOME: Although the court agreed that the employee's initial termination was illegal, it held that her appeal of the second termination should have been dismissed. It therefore reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded with directions to enter judgment in favor of the commission and the chairman.

Lubin v. Agora, Inc.


No. 128, September Term, 2003


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


389 Md. 1; 882 A.2d 833; 2005 Md. LEXIS 544; 33 Media L. Rep. 2366



September 12, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case No. 24-C-03-003540. Robert Hammerman, JUDGE.
Sec. Comm'r v. Agora, 380 Md. 230, 844 A.2d 427, 2004 Md. LEXIS 126 (2004)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court issued a writ of certiorari before intermediate court review of petitioner Securities Commissioner's appeal from a Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) denial of her motion to enforce subpoenas for subscriber lists for respondent publisher's newsletter. The Commissioner claimed a compelling need to learn whether the Maryland Securities Act, Md. Code Ann. Corps. & Ass'ns § 11-101 et seq. (1999 & 2004 Cum. Supp.) had been violated.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner issued the subpoenas because a customer complaint led her to believe that the publisher, not registered as a broker dealer or an investment adviser, was nonetheless operating in that capacity. She argued that interviews with subscribers would enable her to accurately determine whether the law had been violated. The court agreed with the trial court that the Commissioner appeared to be embarking on what amounted to a fishing expedition. She had not convincingly explained why the drastic measure of interfering with subscribers' rights to read and associate with others without being spied upon was the only way she could find out about the publisher's activities. The chilling effect of such disclosure on the subscribers' exercise of their federal and state rights of free speech and association was simply too great to permit enforcement of the subpoenas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

222 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Design Kitchen & Baths v. Lagos


No. 82, September Term, 2003


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


388 Md. 718; 882 A.2d 817; 2005 Md. LEXIS 545



September 12, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Louise Scriviner, JUDGE.
Design Kitchen v. Lagos, 378 Md. 176, 835 A.2d 1103, 2003 Md. LEXIS 772 (2003)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: While review was pending, the court granted certiorari to an appeal by petitioners, an employer and its insurer, from a Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) grant of respondent injured employee's cross-motion for summary judgment upholding a determination of the Maryland Workers' Compensation Commission that the employee, an undocumented alien, was a covered employee within the meaning of Md. Code Ann., Lab. & Empl. § 9-202 (1999).


OVERVIEW: The employee had not lied on his application, but had simply omitted a social security number. This meant that his employment was in violation of federal law, and subjected his employer to potential sanctions under 8 U.S.C.S. § 1324a for failure to verify, among other things, but it did not mean that he was not a covered employee under Md. Code Ann., Lab. & Empl. § 9-202 (1999). Like all remedial statutes, § 9-202 was liberally construed so as to carry out its purpose, and both the plain language of § 9-202 and its legislative history made it clear that coverage of both legal and illegal employees was intended. A federal case relied on by the employer was distinguished as having involved an alien who had forged his documents and then sought back pay for alleged wrongful discharge. This employee was simply seeking protections to which all injured workers were entitled. Nothing in the federal statute indicated an intent to preempt the area.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment.

Wynn v. State


No. 115, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


388 Md. 423; 879 A.2d 1097; 2005 Md. LEXIS 477



August 11, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). Criminal Case No. 96149. Durke G. Thompson, JUDGE.
Wynn v. State, 384 Md. 449, 863 A.2d 997, 2004 Md. LEXIS 878 (2004)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted defendant's petition for a writ of certiorari, allowing defendant to challenge the decision of the Special Court of Appeals (Maryland), which reversed a circuit court decision that had dismissed two charges against defendant that were not re-filed by the State within the time period proscribed in the scheduling order that was issued.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with assault, use of a handgun in the commission of a felony or a crime of violence, and transporting a handgun in a vehicle. He was convicted of transporting a handgun in a vehicle by a jury, but the jury had become deadlocked on the other two charges and the circuit court declared a mistrial. A scheduling order was issued that required the State to decide whether or not to proceed on the two charges within 30 days. The State never refiled the charges, and the circuit court found the failure to comply with its scheduling order fatal and, thereafter, dismissed the charges. Defendant asserted that it was within the circuit court's inherent power to have dismissed the charges. However, the court disagreed and held that the trial court erred when it dismissed the two charges. The court noted that a court's inherent power was to ensure the performance of a judicial function but that the power to sanction violations of scheduling orders by dismissing prosecutions was not necessary for the performance of the judicial function.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Md. State Bd. of Educ. v. Bradford


No. 85, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


387 Md. 353; 875 A.2d 703; 2005 Md. LEXIS 309



June 9, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case Nos. 94340058/CE189672 and 95258055/CL202151. Joseph H.H. Kaplan, JUDGE.
State Bd. of Educ. v. Bradford, 383 Md. 569, 861 A.2d 60, 2004 Md. LEXIS 739 (2004)



DISPOSITION: PARAGRAPHS 10, 11, AND 13 OF ORDER OF AUGUST 20, 2004 ENTERED BY CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY VACATED; COSTS TO BE PAID 3/4 BY APPELLANTS, 1/4 BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Maryland State Board of Education, challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which ordered the State to repay an $ 8 million loan to appellees, the Baltimore City Public School district and others (BCPS), declared that 2004 Md. Laws 288 § 4 was unconstitutional, and made other rulings. The court granted the State certiorari to proceed with its appeal in the declaratory action.


OVERVIEW: The case involved an 11-year battle between the State and the BCPS with regard to the State providing public school funding. Prior caselaw precedent had established that the State was not constitutionally obligated to provide uniformity in funding among the various local school districts and that political subdivisions were not precluded from providing local funds to supplement basic State funding. The State had filed a motion seeking a declaration that State aid provided to the BCPS satisfied the constitutional standard of adequacy. The court found that the portion of the order requiring that the BCPS to receive repayment of the $ 8 million loan balance was immediately appealable under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-303(3)(v), but the State did not complain about that portion of the order. The only portion of the order that was properly before the court was the trial court directive that declared 2004 Md. Laws 288 § 4 unconstitutional. The court held that ch. 288, which required the BCPS to eliminate its $ 58 million deficit, was constitutional and that the trial court order directing the BCPS not to comply was void.


OUTCOME: The court vacated three paragraphs of the order of the trial court which ordered the BCPS not to comply with a particular statute. Otherwise, the court refused to express any opinion as to the rest of the order of the trial court.

 

225 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Consumer Prot. Div. v. Morgan


No. 4, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


387 Md. 125; 874 A.2d 919; 2005 Md. LEXIS 264



May 13, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. John F. Fader, II, JUDGE.
Consumer Prot. v. Morgan, 380 Md. 617, 846 A.2d 401, 2004 Md. LEXIS 199 (2004)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REMAND THIS ACTION TO THE CONSUMER PROTECTION DIVISION WITH DIRECTIONS TO VACATE ITS ORDER OF OCTOBER 22, 2002 IN PART AND TO ENTER A NEW ORDER CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID FORTY PERCENT BY MORGAN, FORTY PERCENT BY SHPRITZ, TEN PERCENT BY ALMONY, AND TEN PERCENT BY THE CONSUMER PROTECTION DIVISION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In petitioner Maryland Attorney General's Consumer Protection Division's proceeding under the Maryland Consumer Protection Act, Md. Code Ann., Com. Law §§ 13-101 through 13-501 (2000 & 2004 Cum. Supp.), against defendant real estate professionals, the court granted certiorari before the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland could consider both sides' appeals of a trial court's partial affirmance and partial reversal of the Division's decision.


OVERVIEW: The professionals--sellers, lenders, and appraisers--were found by the Division to have misrepresented both the value of homes sold and the qualifications of largely low-income buyers in order to obtain federally insured mortgages, on which many buyers defaulted. The court found substantial evidence in the administrative record supporting the Division's determination of the professionals' liability, noting that no showing of scienter was required under the Act. The one area in which the Division had erred was in applying principles of joint and several liability too broadly. Where restitution was ordered, joint and several obligations were proper only where they were based on findings of actions in concert but not where the wrongful misrepresentations were simply concurrent. Therefore, one appraiser who was not really part of the organized scheme should have been liable only for restitution as to transactions in which he was involved. Since the restitution was going to individual buyers, it was only to be granted to those who testified to actual reliance on the misrepresentations. There was no denial of jury trial rights or due process in a standard administrative proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and reversed in part the trial court's judgment and instructed that court, after remand, to remand to the Division after vacating its order, with instructions to enter a new order. The primary net changes from the original order were to limit joint and several liability for restitution awards and to limit individual restitution awards to those who testified to reliance on the misrepresentations.

Bienkowski v. Brooks


No. 34, September Term, 2003


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


386 Md. 516; 873 A.2d 1122; 2005 Md. LEXIS 182



April 11, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County) Michael E. Loney, Pamela L. North, Joseph P. Manck, JUDGES.
Brooks v. Bienkowski, 150 Md. App. 87, 818 A.2d 1198, 2003 Md. App. LEXIS 12 (2003)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED. JUDGMENT OF THE COURT IN BANC FOR THE FIFTH JUDICIAL CIRCUIT REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT IN BANC WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE EQUALLY DIVIDED BETWEEN THE PARTIES. COSTS IN THE COURT IN BANC TO BE PAID BY THE PLAINTIFF BIENKOWKSI.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death action by plaintiff widower against defendant driver, the court granted certiorari review to an appeal by the widower from a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland that reversed an order of a panel of the circuit court in banc and reinstated a trial court's denial of a new trial on the issue of damages only. The court on its own motion further considered whether the intermediate court had appellate jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The widower sought a new trial on the issue of damages only after a jury's award failed to include non-economic losses or loss of household services. The court in banc granted a new trial, and the driver appealed to the intermediate court. Although it reversed the intermediate court's judgment as made without appellate jurisdiction, the court concurred in the result, finding that the trial judge had not abused his discretion in determining that if a new trial were granted to the widower it would have to encompass liability as well as damages. The ruling on jurisdiction was based on the plain language of Md. Const. art. IV, § 22, which referred only to the court of appeals and had never been amended, when other constitutional provisions were, after establishment of the intermediate court. It also accorded with the general rule in Maryland that each appellant received just one appeal as of right, and that the widower had taken his appeal to the court in banc, with certiorari review available in the court's discretion in appropriate cases. If an appeal was mistakenly filed, the intermediate court could simply transfer it for certiorari consideration.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the intermediate court and reversed the judgment of the court in banc. It remanded the matter to the court in banc with directions to affirm the trial court's judgment and order. It also directed its standing committee on rules to recommend rule changes to effectuate its holding in future cases.

 

227 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Rios v. Montgomery County


No. 71, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


386 Md. 104; 872 A.2d 1; 2005 Md. LEXIS 178



April 7, 2005, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Ciruit Court for Montgomery County). Patrick L. Woodward, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor, by his mother, appealed a Maryland Court of Special Appeals affirmance of a dismissal for failure to provide timely notice of claim of his medical malpractice action against defendant county that employed the physician who delivered him. He challenged the constitutionality of the Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-304 (2002 & 2004 Cum. Supp.) time limit and argued that he had shown good cause for waiver of the requirement.


OVERVIEW: Almost 10 years after the alleged negligence of a physician who delivered the minor at a county clinic caused him injuries, his mother, who had been an illegal alien, with little English, finally pursued legal action on his behalf. The § 5-304 time limit for providing notice of claim had expired 180 days after the birth, and the statute did not contain a tolling provision for actions by minors. The court agreed with both lower courts that this provision did not violate equal protection because it bore a rational relationship to local government's need to learn quickly and act on potential claims against it. It did not deny him substantive due process because he had no vested property right in a tort action. His Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 19 right of access to the courts was also subject to reasonable restrictions, particularly in the case of rights created entirely by statute, which could be made subject to conditions precedent. Finally, there was no abuse of discretion in the finding that neither the minor's minority status per se, nor the totality of the circumstances including the adverse circumstances confronted by his mother, constituted good cause for such a long delay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Atty. Griev. Comm'n v. James


Misc. Docket AG No. 1, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


385 Md. 637; 870 A.2d 229; 2005 Md. LEXIS 116



March 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at In re James, 2006 D.C. App. LEXIS 625 (D.C., Nov. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Dwight Davis Jackson, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Attorney disbarred.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent attorney filed several exceptions to findings of fact and conclusions of law by the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which determined that clear and convincing evidence supported a disciplinary petition filed by petitioner, the Attorney Grievance Commission of Maryland through its Bar Counsel, and which recommended the sanction of disbarment after the matter was referred under Md. R. 16-752(a), 16-757(c).


OVERVIEW: The bar counsel brought a disciplinary petition alleging that the attorney's misappropriation of client funds, failure to communicate with clients, and failure to respond to the bar counsel's letters constituted multiple violations of the rules and statutes governing attorney conduct. The court referred the petition to the circuit court for an evidentiary hearing, findings of fact, and conclusions. The circuit court found that clear and convincing evidence demonstrated that the attorney violated Md. R. Prof. Conduct 1.1, 1.3, 1.4, 1.15(a), 8.1(b), 8.4; Md. R. 16-604, 16-607, 16-609; and Md. Code Ann., Bus. Occ. & Prof. §§ 10-304, 10-306. The bar counsel recommended disbarment. The attorney filed exceptions. The court found that the attorney clearly did not act competently in pursuing a cause of action that had no legal basis and in failing to communicate with the client. Also, the attorney misappropriated client funds that were in escrow, failed to put other funds in escrow, and used client finds for personal purposes. Intentional misappropriation of client funds warranted disbarment where the circuit court did not find any factors in mitigation and the attorney did not offer any.


OUTCOME: The court disbarred the attorney.

 

229 of 744 DOCUMENTS


State v. Manck


Misc. No. 1, September Term 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


385 Md. 581; 870 A.2d 196; 2005 Md. LEXIS 114



March 15, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Prohibition, Mandamus, or Other Appropriate Extraordinary Relief. Pamela L. North, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] PETITION FOR WRIT OF PROHIBITION, MANDAMUS OR OTHER EXTRAORDINARY RELIEF DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition for a writ of prohibition, mandamus, or other extraordinary relief in response to the decision of the Anne Arundel County trial court (Maryland) to strike the notice of intention to seek the penalty of death the State filed with regard to defendant. Defendant had been convicted of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from the death of a fellow inmate. Defendant filed his motion to strike the State's notice, arguing that the State constitutionally was prohibited from seeking the death penalty against him because not all of the elements of the crime required for defendant to have been eligible for death were considered by the grand jury and contained in the indictment. Specifically, defendant contended that he was not eligible for the death penalty because the indictment failed to allege that he was a first degree principal. Upon reconsideration, the trial court granted the motion to strike as well as postponed the case to permit the State time to obtain a new indictment and to file a new notice. However, instead of obtaining a new indictment, the State filed its petition seeking prerogatory relief. The court held that it had no jurisdiction over the petition filed by the State, because the State was unable to appeal the trial judge's grant of the motion to strike.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the State's petition for a writ of prohibition, mandamus, or other extraordinary relief.

Schwartz v. Md. Dep't of Natural Res.


No. 94 September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


385 Md. 534; 870 A.2d 168; 2005 Md. LEXIS 112



March 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 1, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case No. CV-8746 Case No. CV-8746. John W. Sause, Jr., JUDGE
Schwartz v. DNR, 383 Md. 569, 861 A.2d 60, 2004 Md. LEXIS 746 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant yacht owners appealed a tax assessment, under Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 8-716 (2000 Repl. Vol), by appellee Maryland Department of Natural Resources. The Secretary of the Department of Natural Resources upheld the assessment. The owners filed for review in the Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County (Maryland). The circuit court reversed the decision and remanded the case with instructions to dismiss the appeal. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners bought a new yacht from a yacht dealership in Maryland. The owners indicated on a Department form that the vessel would be used principally in the State of Florida and would be kept in Florida. Based on their execution of the form, the owners did not pay the Maryland excise tax, due at the time of purchase, on the sale of the vessel in Maryland. Because the Department observed the vessel in Maryland for months after the purchase, the Department issued a tax assessment to the owners, stating that the vessel had incurred the Maryland excise tax liability. The owners contended that the vessel was in Maryland for necessary maintenance and repair before they moved it to Florida. The Department argued that the vessel did not qualify for the Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 8-716(c) exemption as it was not timely removed from Maryland. On appeal, the court found that, because substantial evidence supported the Secretary's findings and inferences, the Secretary did not err in deciding that the vessel was used principally in Maryland in the calendar year under Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 8-701(n) (2000 Repl. Vol). Therefore, the owners were required to pay the Maryland excise tax.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was vacated, and the case was remanded to the circuit court with instructions to affirm the order of the Secretary of the Maryland Department of Natural Resources.

Kushell v. Dep't of Natural Res.


No. 96 September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


385 Md. 563; 870 A.2d 186; 2005 Md. LEXIS 113



March 14, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case No. 02-C-03-092786 AA. Michele D. Jaklitsch, JUDGE.
Kushell v. DNR, 383 Md. 569, 861 A.2d 60, 2004 Md. LEXIS 743 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which entered judgment in favor of appellee Maryland Department of Natural Resources (DNR) by upholding a tax assessment on a boat.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer purchased the boat for use in California. The DNR contended that the taxpayer owed taxes on the boat under Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 8-716(c)(1)(iv) (Cum. Supp. 2001). The taxpayer paid under protest. The circuit court upheld the decision of the DNR, and the taxpayer sought review. In reversing, the court determined that a de novo review was appropriate on the agency's conclusions of law. The court used the well-established rules of statutory interpretation in making its decision. It found that the ordinary rules of English grammar supported the taxpayer's interpretation that intent was a requirement under § 8-716(c)(1)(iv). The interpretation of the DNR would have required a rewriting of the statute. Further, the interpretation asserted by the taxpayer did not render § 8-716(f) superfluous. The parties agreed that, at the time the taxpayer purchased the boat, he had no intention of principally using it in Maryland. Accordingly, he had no tax liability under § 8- 716(c)(1)(iv).


OUTCOME: The decision of the circuit court was reversed. The case was remanded with instructions to reverse the order of the DNR.

 

232 of 744 DOCUMENTS


McDermott v. Dougherty


No. 58, September Term, 2004


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


385 Md. 320; 869 A.2d 751; 2005 Md. LEXIS 105



March 10, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Harford County). Thomas E. Marshall, JUDGE.
McDermott v. Dougherty, 382 Md. 688, 856 A.2d 724, 2004 Md. LEXIS 586 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari to hear petitioner father's appeal from an affirmance, by the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland, of a trial court's judgment awarding sole legal and physical custody of the father's son to respondent maternal grandparents. The father argued that his employment at sea was not cause to deny him custody, particularly in light of the trial court's failure to find him an unfit parent.


OVERVIEW: After the parents divorced and the mother's substance problems resulted in incarceration, the father tried to care for his son, with whom he had a close bond, but he had to return to his career as a merchant marine captain. He accepted the grandparents' help in caring for the son, not knowing the mother had given them an ex parte authorization to exercise custody in her stead. When he returned, he resumed physical custody, but when he once again had to return to sea, he made other arrangements to have the son remain with the couple who had kept house for both of them while he was at home. The grandparents sought custody, and the trial court found that such an award was in the son's best interest. The court of appeals clarified that the true rule in Maryland was the one followed in the majority of states, that a best interests analysis was inappropriate in the fact of a fit parent's constitutional and common law right to raise his child. Although that presumption of a fit parent's right to custody could be overcome by exceptional circumstances, the fact that the father's occupation required absences, during which he had made appropriate arrangements, was not such a circumstance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the intermediate court. It remanded the matter to that court with instructions to reverse the trial court judgment and to remand the case to the trial court for further proceedings, particularly regarding the father's petition for an award of attorney fees. Appellate costs were to be paid by the grandparents.
