Office of the Governor v. Washington Post Co.


No. 117, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


360 Md. 520; 759 A.2d 249; 2000 Md. LEXIS 591



September 12, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Lawrence H. Rushworth, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. PETITIONERS TO PAY TWO THIRDS OF THE COSTS AND RESPONDENT TO PAY ONE THIRD OF THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court issued a writ of certiorari after the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) stayed the trial court's judgment from which defendants, governor and his office, had appealed in plaintiff newspaper's Maryland Public Information Act, Md. Code Ann., State Gov't §§ 10-611 to 10-630, suit to obtain from defendants phone and appointment records covering a six month period which defendants had refused to give.


OVERVIEW: Under the Maryland Public Information Act (Act), Md. Code Ann., State Gov't §§ 10-611 to 10-630, plaintiff newspaper asked defendant governor's office for appointment records and all phone records of defendant governor and some of his staff for a six month period. Defendant office provided plaintiff only the aggregate cost figure for such calls, and defendant governor's public agendas. Plaintiff sued. After in camera review, the trial court ordered defendants to comply and they appealed. The appellate court stayed the trial judgment and the court issued a writ of certiorari and vacated and remanded. The Act established a general presumption in favor of disclosure. Although content of calls may have been private, phone bills for official calls were not. The factual records sought were not generally subject to executive privilege, or were they personnel records, confidential commercial information, or interagency memos. Defendants had the chance on remand to show certain records to be privileged and have them redacted. Phone records from the governor's mansion and from phones which defendant governor and the other staff had likely used very little if at all were nondisclosable.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court was vacated and the case remanded for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion. The factual records sought were generally not subject to executive privilege or other public information act exemptions, though defendants on remand could try to show them to be. Phone records from defendant governor's home and from phones which he and the other staff had likely used very little were nondisclosable.

Montgomery County v. Broad. Equities, Inc.


No. 141, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


360 Md. 438; 758 A.2d 995; 2000 Md. LEXIS 589



September 8, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). William P. Turner, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED AND CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO VACATE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO DISMISS THE ACTION. EACH SIDE TO PAY ITS OWN COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants petitioned and plaintiff cross-petitioned for a writ of certiorari to review of a decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed in part and reversed in part a circuit court decision in an action seeking declaratory judgment and injunctive relief blocking an administrative proceeding enforcing Montgomery County, Md., Code § 27-18(b). The court granted both the petition and the cross-petition.


OVERVIEW: One of plaintiff's former employees filed an administrative complaint alleging plaintiff violated Montgomery County, Md., Code § 27-18(b) by firing the employee because of his sexual orientation. Defendant commission investigated the complaint then instituted proceedings against plaintiff. While those proceedings were pending, plaintiff filed the instant action challenging the validity of several county code provisions and seeking an injunction enjoining defendants from proceeding with the administrative hearing. The circuit court ruled against plaintiff. The special appeals court affirmed that decision in part and reversed in part. The instant court vacated the special appeal's court's decision and remanded with instructions. Plaintiff's case did not fall within the Harbor Island "constitutional" exception to the normal rule that primary administrative and judicial review remedies must be exhausted; plaintiff did not challenge the regulatory scheme "as a whole," and resolution of the instant case would not terminate the parties' controversy.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the special appeals court vacated and case remanded with instructions. Plaintiff's action was to be dismissed because plaintiff failed to exhaust his administrative remedies before resorting to judicial intervention in the dispute.

Manikhi v. Mass Transit Admin.


No. 106, September Term, 1999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


360 Md. 333; 758 A.2d 95; 2000 Md. LEXIS 517



August 24, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 1, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Case No. 97073040/CC437. Robert I. H. Hammerman, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS ON COUNT II (FALSE IMPRISONMENT) REVERSED AS TO RESPONDENT, FRANCISCO OVID, ON COUNT V (TITLE VII) REVERSED AS TO THE RESPONDENT, MASS TRANSIT ADMINISTRATION, AND ON COUNTS VII (§ 1983) AND XII (MARYLAND CONSTITUTION) REVERSED AS TO THE RESPONDENTS, WADE MORAGNE-EL AND VERNON PARSONS; CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AS TO THOSE COUNTS AND RESPONDENTS WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND THIS ACTION AS TO THOSE COUNTS AND RESPONDENTS TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; AS TO ALL OTHER COUNTS, UNNUMBERED CLAIMS, AND PARTIES, THE JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS IS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the Court of Special Appeals' (Maryland) judgment affirming the trial court's grant of respondents' motion to dismiss her amended complaint. The court granted certiorari review to assess the legal sufficiency of petitioner's allegations of false imprisonment, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000e et seq., 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and Md. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 24.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee sued respondents, employer, co-worker, supervisors, and union officials, for sexual harassment. The trial court dismissed petitioner's amended complaint. The intermediate appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision, and petitioner appealed. The court granted petitioner's request for certiorari to assess the legal sufficiency of her allegations of false imprisonment, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and violations of Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964 (Title VII), as amended, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000e et seq., 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and Md. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 24. The dismissal of petitioner's false imprisonment claim was reversed as to respondent co-worker, as respondent co-worker's conduct deprived petitioner of her liberty, without her consent, and without legal justification. The dismissal of petitioner's Title VII claim was reversed as to respondent employer, as respondent co-worker's conduct created a hostile work environment which was imputable to respondent employer. Finally, the dismissal of petitioner's § 1983 and Md. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 24 claims were reversed as to respondent supervisors.


OUTCOME: The judgment affirming the dismissal of petitioner's false imprisonment claim was reversed as to respondent co-worker. The judgment affirming the dismissal of petitioner's Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, as amended, claim was reversed as to respondent employer. The judgment affirming the dismissal of petitioner's equal protection claims under the federal and Maryland Constitutions was reversed as to respondent supervisors.

 

351 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Metheny v. State


No. 149, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


359 Md. 576; 755 A.2d 1088; 2000 Md. LEXIS 446



July 24, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 10, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Death Penalty - Circuit Court for Baltimore County. James T. Smith, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE OF DEATH VACATED; JUDGMENTS OTHERWISE AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY FOR NEW SENTENCING PROCEEDINGS; COSTS TO BE PAID BY MAYOR AND COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE CITY. Dissenting opinion follows:.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Md. Code Ann. § 414 (1999 Supp.) and Md. R. App. Review, Ct. App. and Ct. Spec. App. 8-306(c)(1), defendant appealed his sentence to death, imposed after defendant pled guilty to pre-meditated murder and robbery in the Circuit Court of Baltimore County (Maryland).


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to first-degree premeditated murder and robbery, but prayed a jury for the sentencing phase. The jury sentenced appellant to death based on its apparently unanimous finding of the aggravating circumstance that the murder was committed while appellant was committing a robbery. The trial judge imposed the death sentence and a concurrent prison sentence for the robbery conviction. Execution of the death sentence was stayed pending appellate review pursuant to Md. Code Ann. § 414 (1999 Supp.) and Md. R. App. Review, Ct. App. and Ct. Spec. App. 8-306(c)(1). The appellate court affirmed the sentence for the robbery, holding that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in finding an adequate factual basis to support the guilty plea to robbery, including appellant's specific intent to rob the victim. However, the appellate court vacated the death sentence because the evidence, which clearly indicated that the robbery was committed as an afterthought to murder, was insufficient to establish the sole statutory aggravator justifying imposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: Robbery conviction and sentence were affirmed; trial court properly determined factual basis underlying guilty plea. Sentence of death vacated and case remanded because the evidence, which clearly indicated that the robbery was committed as an afterthought to murder, was insufficient to establish the sole statutory aggravator justifying imposition of the death penalty.

 

352 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Harryman v. State


No. 1 September Term, 1999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


359 Md. 492; 754 A.2d 1018; 2000 Md. LEXIS 389



June 29, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Howard County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Raymond J. Kane, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY HOWARD COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland) of constructive criminal contempt for failure to pay child support after that charge had been referred by the circuit court to a master pursuant to Md. R. Family Law Actions 9-207(a)(1)(G).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was delinquent in the payment of child support. The State prosecuted defendant for constructive criminal contempt. The circuit court referred the prosecution for determination by a master pursuant to Md. R. Family Law Actions 9-207(a)(1)(G). The circuit court, relying upon findings of the master, entered judgment convicting defendant. The court reversed that judgment holding that the circuit court had no authority under Md. R. Family Law Actions 9-207(a)(1)(G) or otherwise to refer the constructive criminal contempt prosecution to a master. A constructive criminal contempt prosecution, unlike a constructive civil contempt proceeding, was not to be included in any action in which the alleged contempt occurred, but was to be docketed as a separate criminal action, and carried out by a judge. Whether or not constitutionally mandated, as a matter of sound judicial policy, incarceration was to be ordered only by a judge on a record developed before the judge. In a criminal contempt prosecution additional criminal safeguards of a criminal procedure were to be available to the accused, including the panoply of fundamental due process rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The circuit court had no authority under that rule or otherwise to refer the constructive criminal contempt prosecution to a master. A constructive criminal contempt prosecution, unlike a constructive civil contempt proceeding, was not to be included in any action in which the alleged contempt occurred, but was to be docketed as a separate criminal action, and carried out by a judge.

 

353 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Pollock v. Patuxent Inst. Bd. of Review


No. 91, September Term, 1999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


358 Md. 656; 751 A.2d 496; 2000 Md. LEXIS 247



May 12, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Howard County Case No. 13-C-97-35616 AA.) James B. Dudley, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO VACATE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY AND TO REMAND THIS CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a petition for certiorari to appeal the ruling entered in the Court of Special Appeals, Maryland, which affirmed the denial of his petition for writ of habeas corpus in the Circuit Court for Howard County.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was paroled while serving life sentences for murder and two years consecutive for escape. Respondent then revoked parole. That revocation was reversed by the circuit court and affirmed by the Court of Special Appeals. Petitioner filed a habeas corpus petition in that action for judicial review of the revocation. Petitioner then filed a petition for certiorari, which was granted. Justice required utilizing the habeas corpus proceeding to obtain judicial review of the administrative action in not renewing parole. Although the present proceeding was initiated as a petition for habeas corpus relief directing that petitioner be paroled, respondent injected into the proceeding a defense based on facts that arose after the proceeding was initiated. It was respondent's defense of mootness that opened the door for petitioner to obtain judicial review of the administrative decision.


OUTCOME: The petition for certiorari was granted and the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals was vacated and remanded the lower court. Justice required utilizing the habeas corpus proceeding to obtain judicial review of the administrative action in not renewing parole.

 

354 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Migdal v. State


No. 115, September Term, 1999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


358 Md. 308; 747 A.2d 1225; 2000 Md. LEXIS 111



March 14, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case # Civil 197291. J. James McKenna, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR ENTRY OF A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION; RESPONDENT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petition for writ of certiorari was granted after the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) entered declaratory judgment in favor of respondent state, finding that the statute at issue did not violate the one-subject requirement of Md. Const. Art. III, § 29 as alleged by petitioners, shareholders of mutual funds.


OVERVIEW: Petition for writ of certiorari, filed by petitioner mutual fund shareholders, was granted to review a finding in favor of respondent state, that a statute did not violate the one-subject requirement of Md. Const. Art. III, § 29. Part of the statute had been defeated as a bill, and was engrafted onto another bill which had been unanimously approved. The approved bill's sponsor voted against the engrafted version. The approved bill served to protect individuals from being appointed resident agents without their written consent. The engrafted version additionally provided that directors of certain investment companies would be deemed independent and disinterested. Protecting individuals from being appointed as resident agents without their written consent was not germane to protecting investment company directors' decisions from shareholders' derivative suits. Combining these separate and unrelated provisions into one Act was unconstitutional. The directors' liability provisions were invalid and severed from the resident agent provision.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for entry of a declaratory judgment. The contested statute violated the state constitution's one-subject requirement, rendering provisions that had been engrafted from a defeated bill unconstitutional, null and void.

 

355 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Burch v. State


No. 56, September Term, 1999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


358 Md. 278; 747 A.2d 1209; 2000 Md. LEXIS 107



March 13, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW OF DENIAL OF APPELLANT FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL FROM FINAL JUDGMENT (DEATH PENALTY, Circuit Court for Prince George's County). Case No. CT950787X. Steven I. Platt, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which denied his motion for reconsideration of defendant's death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death by a jury for the murders of two people. The appellate court affirmed the verdict and one of the two death sentences. Defendant requested the trial court to reconsider his sentence. The trial court ruled it had no authority to modify the sentence. The appellate court agreed. The issue before the appellate court was whether the trial judge properly concluded that he had no authority under Md. R. Crim. Causes 4-345(b) to modify a jury-determined sentence of death. The court held that when a judge imposed a sentence of death in accordance with a jury determination, Rule 4-345(b) was inapplicable and the circuit court had no authority under that rule to modify the sentence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Circuit court did not have authority to modify jury-determined death sentence.

 

356 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Prince George's County v. Beretta U.S.A. Corp.


No. 110, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


358 Md. 166; 747 A.2d 647; 2000 Md. LEXIS 106; 82 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 477



March 9, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County). G.R. Hovey Johnson, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO DISMISS THE APPEAL. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY BERETTA U.S.A. CORP.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer and appellee county challenged judgment of Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which held that appellant was entitled to appeal lower court's decision regarding the validity of a local ordinance concerning employment discrimination and subsequently invalidating the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employer sought to overturn appellee county's decision that appellant's discharge of a former employee was retaliation discrimination and awarding the former employee damages under Prince George's County, Md. Code § 2-195.01(a)(3). The lower court had concluded that appellant was entitled to appeal because appellant could have brought a declaratory or mandamus action to challenge the validity of appellee's discrimination ordinance. The appellate court concluded that appellate review was precluded because neither the language of Md. Code Ann. Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-302(a) and the case law on which it was based, nor the local ordinance provided for appellate review. The availability of an alternative judicial action did not authorize the lower court to entertain the appeal because there was no exception to the non-appealability doctrine embodied in Md. Code Ann. Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-302(a) for issues that could have been litigated in some alternative judicial proceeding.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed because statutory codification of non-appealability doctrine precluded review and did not provide an exception for issues that could have been litigated in some alternative judicial proceeding.

 

357 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Doe


No. 99, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


358 Md. 113; 747 A.2d 617; 2000 Md. LEXIS 99



March 7, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 8, 2000. As Corrected March 31, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore County). Christian M. Kahl, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY. RESPONDENT TO PAY THE COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the decision of the Court of Special Appeals, which reversed the holding of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County, Maryland, which dismissed respondent's actions for fraud and intentional infliction of emotional distress against his wife.


OVERVIEW: After discovering that two of his three children were fathered by his wife's art professor, respondent husband filed for divorce, and sought damages for fraud and intentional infliction of emotional distress resulting from petitioner wife's alleged adultery and misrepresentation of the paternity of the children. The trial court dismissed the tort counts, holding that those causes of action were barred by interspousal immunity and by public policy. The intermediate court reversed. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that respondent's tort claims were not viable. Respondent sought to recover damages, under different tort labels, for the same type of conduct that formerly gave rise to the common law cause of action known as "criminal conversation." That action was abolished on constitutional and public policy grounds years before. The identical public policy considerations were applicable here. Allowing respondent's actions would simply be reviving the tort of criminal conversation through artful pleading.


OUTCOME: Intermediate court reversed; the public policy of the state, reflected in the abolition of the actions for alienation of affections and criminal conversation, required dismissal of the tort actions asserted by respondent.

 

358 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Save Our Streets v. Mitchell


No. 102, September Term, 1998, No. 104, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


357 Md. 237; 743 A.2d 748; 2000 Md. LEXIS 2



January 10, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 102. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. James C. Chapin, JUDGE.

104. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Harford County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. William O. Carr, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged orders of the Montgomery County Circuit Court and the Hartford County Circuit Court (Maryland) that precluded the placement of proposed charter amendments on the ballots for a general election.


OVERVIEW: After trial on the controversy, the trial court issued a declaratory judgment precluding the placement of the proposed charter amendment on the general election ballot. The appellate court affirmed the lower court's ruling by finding that the proposed amendment was essentially legislative in character and in all respects similar to the enactment of a local law. As such, it was an improper attempt to divest the county government of its power to legislate. While charters commonly authorized or precluded specified types of enactments by legislative bodies, they did not properly contain all provisions concerning the subject. The proposed speed bump amendment would narrowly have mandated that the county council could not authorize new speed bumps, and that it must remove all in existence. Thus, the proposed amendment left virtually no room for the exercise of discretion by the county council.


OUTCOME: The trial court order precluding the inclusion of a proposed charter amendment was affirmed where the proposal was an improper attempt to divest the county's governing officials of their power to legislate.

 

359 of 744 DOCUMENTS


City of Annapolis v. Waterman


No. 37, September Term, 1999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


357 Md. 484; 745 A.2d 1000; 2000 Md. LEXIS 1



January 7, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 11, 2000. As Corrected January 18, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case # C-1996-30475.OC. Michael E. Loney, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY REVERSED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), finding that conditions imposed on appellee's property constituted an impermissible taking.


OVERVIEW: Appellees filed suit alleging that certain conditions contained in the subdivision approval, which was applicable to their property, constituted an unconstitutional taking of that property. The trial court found that appellant had impermissibly conditioned approval of appellee's subdivision proposal. On appeal, the issues decided were whether the lower court erred in finding two conditions constituted a "dedication," whether the "non-segmentation" principle should have been applied in the takings analysis, and whether a taking had occurred, notwithstanding that appellees had not lost all economically viable use of their property. The court held that the trial court erred when it used an exactions analysis to reverse appellant city council's decision with respect to the conditions imposed. Thus, because no unconstitutional taking of appellees' property occurred, the court reversed.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed because the lower court erred when it applied an exactions analysis to property dedicated by appellees.

Burke v. State


No. 2388, September Term, 2014


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


2016 Md. App. LEXIS 888

Long v. Md. State Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr. Servs.


No. 2593, September Term, 2014


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


230 Md. App. 1; 146 A.3d 546; 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 112



September 28, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 2593, Sept. Term, 2014 Filed: September 28, 2016 Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Sharon V. Burrell, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court properly granted the Maryland Department of Public Safety and Correctional Services' motion for summary judgment and ruling that a sex offender had to register for life in accordance with Crim. Proc. § 11-707(a)(2)(i) and (4)(iii) (2015 Supp.) because there was nothing whatsoever in the record to support the offender's argument that when he pled guilty, he was promised that he would only have to register for 10 years; [2]-The circuit court properly ruled, pursuant to the intent-effects test, that the registration requirements in Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 11-706(a) (2014) did not violate Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 17 because the added burdens brought about by the 2009 or 2010 amendments to the Maryland Sex Offender Registration Act did not constitute punishment.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Shiflett v. State


No. 2198, September Term, 2014


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


229 Md. App. 645; 146 A.3d 504; 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 113



September 28, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Shiflett v. State, 2017 Md. LEXIS 228 (Md., Apr. 21, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 2198, Sept. Term, 2014 Filed: September 28, 2016 Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County. Ruth Ann Jakubowski, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court properly ordered defendant to wear a stun cuff as a condition of being present in the courtroom because he repeatedly threatened the judge and the prosecutor, he defecated on the floor of his cell in a temporarily successful effort to prevent the trial from proceeding, he screamed the judge's name from outside her chambers until he was forcibly restrained, and he sent the judge inappropriate, vulgar letters at her home address; [2]-The court properly excluded an expert's testimony under Md. R. 5-702 after concluding that there was no nexus between defendant's psychological profile and the specific intent required to prove first-degree murder; the testimony lacked an adequate factual basis, and had no relevance to any material issue or defense in the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Action Comm. for Transit, Inc. v. Town of Chevy Chase


No. 1204, September Term, 2015


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


229 Md. App. 540; 145 A.3d 640; 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 102; 44 Media L. Rep. 2249



September 1, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Cheryl A. McCally, Judge.
Montgomery Cnty. v. Bhatt, 443 Md. 234, 116 A.3d 474, 2015 Md. LEXIS 416 (2015)



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY IS VACATED AND THIS CASE REMANDED TO IT FOR PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. APPELLEE TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court erred in granting summary judgment to a town in an action by a public-interest group and a blogger for a waiver of fees under Md. Gen. Prov. Code Ann. § 4-206 (2014), because the town's response failed to identify what relevant factors the custodian considered, including the group's previous criticism of the town officials for their opposition to a proposed light rail public transit system, and the blogger's activities made him a member of the "media" for purposes of Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 9-112(a).


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated and case remanded.

 

380 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. State


No. 0168, September Term, 2015


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


229 Md. App. 385; 145 A.3d 105; 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 94



August 31, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Kent County. Ernest Broughton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR KENT COUNTY VACATED, AND THE CASE IS REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID 3/4 BY APPELLANT AND 1/4 BY KENT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court properly denied defendant's motion to dismiss charges against him under Md. Code Ann., Crim. Proc. § 6-103 (2001, 2008 Repl. Vol., 2015 Supp.) and Md. R. 4-271 based upon a Hicks violation, as defendant had requested a competency evaluation, and waiting for the results constituted good cause to delay the trial; [2]-Defendant's conviction for possession of a shotgun by a prohibited person under Md. Code Ann., Pub. Safety § 5-205 did not violate the retroactive restrictions clause of Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 17 because it was not retrospective, as defendant was not being punished for conduct that occurred prior to its enactment; [3]-The trial court abused its discretion in failing to ask a requested "strong feelings" voir dire question regarding § 5-205 because it went directly to the charge and would have been helpful in uncovering biases.


OUTCOME: Judgments vacated; matter remanded for further proceedings, including new trial.

 

381 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Bellard v. State


No. 1281, September Term, 2014


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


229 Md. App. 312; 145 A.3d 61; 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 97



August 31, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted Bellard v. State, 450 Md. 660, 150 A.3d 817, 2016 Md. LEXIS 812 (Dec. 2, 2016)
Affirmed by Bellard v. State, 2017 Md. LEXIS 196 (Md., Mar. 31, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Dwight Jackson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY VACATED AS TO TWO CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES FOR CONSPIRACY TO COMMIT MURDER AND AFFIRMED IN ALL OTHER RESPECTS. COSTS ASSESSED 22% TO PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AND 78% TO APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The State was authorized by Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 2-203 to serve notice of its intent to seek a sentence of imprisonment for life without the possibility of parole for defendant's first-degree murder charges, and as legislation had repealed the death penalty, defendant's sentencing procedures were governed by Md. Code Ann., Crim. Law § 2-304(a) and Md. R. 4-342, such that he was not entitled to elect to be sentenced by a jury; [2]-It was error to convict defendant of three counts of conspiracy to commit murder, arising out of a quadruple murder, because the evidence supported only one conspiracy involving the murder of three people, and the State did not allege, and the jury was not instructed to make a determination, that defendant entered into more than one conspiracy.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated as to two convictions and sentences for conspiracy to commit murder. Remainder of judgment affirmed.

385 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Colbert v. State


No. 2332, September Term, 2014


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


229 Md. App. 79; 143 A.3d 173; 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 84



July 28, 2016, Filed



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1(c) did not violate the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV, as fell within Justice Kennedy's McNeely concurrence and it helped law enforcement identify a category of cases in which it was reasonable to dispense with the warrant requirement; [2]-Section 16-205.1(c) required a motor vehicle accident that had caused death or a life threatening injury. As the attention of law enforcement would be divided between critical tasks, it was proper to assign a lower priority to obtaining a warrant before the evidence metabolized; [3]-Section 16-205.1(c) required that law enforcement have an articulable suspicion that the defendant was under the influence of drugs or alcohol; [4]-As the three conditions of § 16-205.1(c) applied, defendant was properly required to submit to a breath test without a warrant.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

391 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Harvey v. Sines


No. 0691, September Term, 2015


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


228 Md. App. 283; 137 A.3d 1045; 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 61



June 2, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Garrett County. Ray Strubin, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR GARRETT COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Maryland Dormant Mineral Interests Act (Act), Md. Code Ann., Envir. § 15-1201 et seq. (2014), did not violate Md. Const. Decl. Rights. art. 24 as it did not retroactively impair vested rights as it provided for a grace period and the dormant mineral interest holders had not used their interests for at least 20 years; [2]-The holders had not exploited their interest for over 102 years and had not paid taxes; [3]-The dormant mineral interests were not automatically extinguished and the holders could record a notice of intent to preserve their interest under Md. Code Ann., Envir. § 15-1204(a) (2014), have a Md. R. 12-704(d) hearing, appeal the termination of their rights and in certain circumstances, file a late notice of intent to use under Md. Code Ann., Envir. § 15-1205 (2014); [5]-The Act did not take property without just compensation under Md. Const. art. III, § 40.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

392 of 744 DOCUMENTS


State v. Braverman


No. 429, September Term, 2015


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


228 Md. App. 239; 137 A.3d 377; 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 58



June 1, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Goldberg v. State, 2016 Md. LEXIS 654 (Md., Sept. 29, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel Count.y Paul F. Harris, JUDGE.
State v. Goldberg, 437 Md. 191, 85 A.3d 231, 2014 Md. LEXIS 134 (2014)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The attorney's fees awarded to a class of ground rent owners against the State of Maryland (State) after the invalidation of 2007 Md. Laws 286 was not supported by 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 as the State was not a person under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983; [2]-The fees could not be awarded under the common-fund doctrine since there was no fund and the fees were to be paid outside any fund; [3]-Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 12-106(b)(5) (2015) did not support the award since the fees were awarded to the plaintiffs and § 12-106(b)(5) did not apply to an inverse condemnation case; [4]-No fees were actually incurred to support the award under § 12-106(b)(5); [5]-The fees were not supported by Md. R. 1-341 since there was a substantial justification for the State's position and neither the owners nor any third parties acting on their behalf had incurred any fees.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

400 of 744 DOCUMENTS


Accokeek, Mattawoman, Piscataway Creeks Cmtys. Council, Inc. v. Md. PSC


No. 2437, September Term, 2014


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


227 Md. App. 265; 133 A.3d 1228; 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 32



March 30, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted Accokeek, Mattawoman, Piscataway Creeks Cmtys. Council v. PSC, 448 Md. 724, 141 A.3d 135, 2016 Md. LEXIS 440 (July 11, 2016)
Affirmed by Accokeek v. PSC of Md., 451 Md. 1, 150 A.3d 856, 2016 Md. LEXIS 839 (Dec. 16, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Accokeek, Mattawoman, Piscataway Creeks Cmtys. Council, Inc. v. Md. PSC, 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 862 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., Feb. 16, 2016)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a review action, the Maryland Public Service Commission's (PSC) decision pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Pub. Util. Cos. §§ 7-207 and 7-208 (1998, 2010 Repl. Vol., 2014 Supp.) to authorize construction of an electric generating station was affirmed, as the PSC made sufficient findings of fact regarding the positive economic effects of the station and it gave due consideration to all the required factors under § 7-207(e)(2)(ii); [2]-Substantial evidence supported the PSC's calculation of economic effects and revenues resulting from the station under § 7-207(e)(2)(ii), based on multiple sources of evidence on that issue; [3]-The PSC's imposition of conditions was within its statutory authority in order to benefit both the environmental and economic interests of the State, as the conditions were not taxes and the primary purpose of the conditions was not revenue.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.
